البائع أن يحبسها بالثمن لم يكن له ذلك لأنه لما باعه منه علمه أن المبيع في يد المشتري وهو يتمكن من القبض يصير راضياً بقبض المشتري دلالة اهـ. وقيد ببيعه ممن يزعم أنه عنده لأنه لو باعه من رجل يزعم أنه عند آخر فإنه لا يصح فاسد إذا قبضه المشتري ملكه بخلاف بيع الآبق فإنه باطل فلذا كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية أن بيع الآبق يكون باطلاً وفاسداً وصحيحاً
Book of Sales, Chapter of Invalid Sale. Because he is not able to deliver it, and if he sold it and then the absconding returns, the contract does not become valid because it occurred void due to absence of locality, like the sale of a bird in the air. And from Abu Hanifa that the contract becomes valid if not rescinded because the contract was concluded due to the existence of value and the obstacle has been removed, which is inability to deliver, just as if it absconds after the sale. And thus it is narrated from Muhammad; likewise in al-Hidayah. And the first is the apparent transmission, and Abu Abdullah al-Balkhi used to give fatwa accordingly, as in al-Dhakhira. And they interpreted that transmission as meaning the conclusion of the sale by mutual giving now. He made it general, so it includes if he sold it to his minor son, for it is not permissible. Likewise the orphan under his guardianship, contrary to if he gifted it to him, for it is permissible. The difference is that the condition of sale is ability to deliver immediately after the sale, and that is absent. And what remains of his possession is suitable for taking possession of a gift, not for taking possession of a sale, because it is taking possession in exchange for property received from the son's property, and this is taking possession not in exchange for property coming out of the child's property. So that possession sufficed for him in consideration of the minor, because if it returns, it returns to the minor's ownership. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tabyin. And in Fatawa Qadikhan regarding gift there is contrary: he said: If he gifted his absconding slave to his minor son, it is not permissible, and if he sold it, it is permissible. So he reversed the ruling according to what the commentators narrated, and I have not seen any of them point out this. The truth is what the judge mentioned because in al-Mi'raj: If he sold the absconder to his minor son, it is not permissible; if he gifted it to him or to an orphan under his guardianship, it is permissible because what remains of his possession over the absconder suffices for taking the gift, not the sale. As for the author of al-Dhakhira, he mentioned in al-Buyu' that if the father sold the slave sent for his need to his minor son, it is permissible, and he did not mention it regarding the absconder. And he mentioned in the Book of Gift: If he gifted a slave who had absconded to his minor son, as long as he is at large in the abode of Islam, the gift is valid and he becomes a possessor for his son by the gift itself; he mentioned this issue in al-Jami'. And in al-Muntaqa from Abu Yusuf: If he gave in charity an absconding slave to his minor son, it is not permissible. And al-Mu'alla narrated from him that it is permissible, so two narrations from Abu Yusuf in this issue. His statement also includes if he sold it after it absconded from the hand of the usurper from him, because in al-Dhakhira: If the usurped slave absconds from the usurper's hand, then the owner sold the slave to the usurper while it is absconding, the sale is valid. The principle is that absconding prevents validity of sale only if delivery is needed, i.e., if it absconds from the owner's hand and then the owner sells it. But if delivery is not needed, as in our issue, the sale is valid. And it is restricted to the absconder because the slave sent for the master's need may be sold. If he sold it while it was not absconding, then it absconds before delivery, the buyer has the option to rescind the contract, and the seller cannot demand the price until the slave is present. And it is made that the return is on the seller, as in al-Qunyah. And the usurped case is excluded: Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that it is suspended; if the usurper acknowledges it, the sale is complete and binding. Also the father: it is valid; he did not differentiate between them if it is during the day, so refer to it. His statement: (And they interpreted that transmission...) This also contradicts what he presented at the beginning of the Book of Sales regarding mutual giving does not constitute a valid contract after a void or invalid sale unless the first contract is rescinded. His statement: (And in Fatawa Qadikhan regarding gift there is contrary) He said in al-Nahr: and it occurs in al-Khaniyah in some copies: It perished until even if he denies it and the owner of the usurped property has fair witnesses, then the answer is the same. If he has no witnesses and he does not surrender it, the sale is rescinded. Some of our scholars said: Muhammad's statement in al-Asl 'if the owner of the usurped property has no witnesses and he does not surrender it until it perishes, the sale is rescinded' is apparently incorrect. The sale should not be rescinded because the sale is lost but has been replaced by a substitute. When the sold item is lost and a substitute is provided, the sale is not rescinded unless the buyer chooses rescission. The interpretation of Muhammad's statement is that the sale is rescinded if the buyer chooses it. Others said it is apparently correct and the sale is rescinded without the buyer's choice, etc., from al-Dhakhira. And it is restricted to his sale because his gift is valid as we presented on al-Mi'raj. As for his emancipation, it is valid, but if he emancipates it for an expiation owed by him, it is not valid until his life is known, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is valid to make it as a substitute for khul' as we presented in its chapter at his statement: 'if she divorces for a consideration on an absconding slave she owns, on condition that she is free from its guarantee, she is not free'. And as for making it a substitute for sulh. His statement: (Except if he sells it to someone who claims it is with him, then the sale is valid because what is prohibited is the sale of an absconder absolutely, i.e., it is absconding with respect to both, and this is not absconding with respect to the buyer. And because if it is with the buyer, the inability to deliver is removed, and that is the obstacle. And the author did not mention that its taking possession suffices for taking possession of the sold item for detail. They said: If he had witnesses at the time of taking it that he took it to return it to its owner, it is an amana in his hand, so it does not substitute for taking possession of the sale. If it perishes before reaching its owner, he is not liable, so the sale is rescinded and he returns to the owner for the price. If he did not have witnesses, he becomes a possessor because it is taking possession by usurpation. This is what the commentators confined to here. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira: If he buys something that is an amana in his hand from a deposit or loan, he does not become a possessor unless the depositor or borrower goes to the item and reaches a place where he is able to take possession now, then the buyer becomes a possessor by khala. If it perishes after that, it perishes from the buyer's property. If the buyer does in the section of deposit and loan what constitutes taking possession, then the seller wants to retain it for the price, he does not have that because when he sold it to him, knowing that the sold item is in the buyer's hand and he can take possession, he becomes satisfied with the buyer's possession by indication. And it is restricted to his sale to someone who claims it is with him because if he sold it to a man who claims it is with another, it is not valid, because [it is] invalid? Actually it says 'it is not valid' but then 'if the buyer takes possession, he owns it' so it is fasid? Then it says 'as opposed to sale of an absconder, for it is batil'. Therefore we wrote in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah that the sale of an absconder is batil, fasid, and sahih.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Raiq commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the sale of a runaway slave (abiq). The default ruling is that such a sale is void (batil) because the seller cannot deliver the slave at the time of contract, analogous to selling a bird in the air. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that if the slave returns before the buyer rescinds, the contract becomes valid because the obstacle (inability to deliver) is removed. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it remains void, and this was the fatwa of Abu Abdullah al-Balkhi. The text then applies this to a father selling to his minor son: since the father lacks full ability to deliver (the slave is not in his custody), the sale is invalid. Gifting to a minor son, however, is valid because the father's existing control suffices for gift (as it is not in exchange for property from the minor). The passage also covers the case of a usurped slave: if the slave escapes from the usurper and the owner sells to the usurper, the sale is valid because delivery is not needed (the usurper already has control). Finally, the exception: if the buyer already has the slave (e.g., as an amana), the sale is valid because there is no inability to deliver. Detailed conditions are given about whether the buyer's possession counts as valid delivery for the sale (it does if he took it without witnesses, i.e., as a usurper; if he took it as an amana, it does not). The text concludes by noting that the sale of an absconder can be batil, fasid, or sahih depending on circumstances.

Key Terms
آبق (ābiq): A slave who has run away from his master.
إباق (ibāq): The act of a slave running away.
تعاطي (ta'āṭī): Mutual giving (offer and acceptance without verbal formula) that can constitute a valid contract in some contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what happens if a person sells a runaway slave and the slave returns before the buyer rescinds?
A) The contract becomes valid.
B) The contract remains void.
C) The contract is suspended until the seller confirms.
D) The buyer must accept the slave.

Key Takeaway
The sale of a runaway slave is bāṭil; even if the slave returns, the contract is not revived, according to the muftā bihi Hanafi position.

Ruling on Selling a Woman's Milk
Ruling statement with commentary on a textual dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a woman's milk and explain why the sale is invalid (batil).

Core Idea
A woman's milk is not property; its sale is invalid in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson addresses a specific issue from the chapter of sales: whether human milk can be sold. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq rules that it is impermissible, and the commentary from Bahr al-Raiq confirms this despite a textual dispute. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of what can be lawfully traded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling a woman's milk. The ruling stated is 'la yajuz' (not permissible). In Hanafi fiqh, this means the sale is invalid (batil).
2
Consider the reasoning
Though the passage is incomplete, the typical Hanafi reasoning is that human milk is not considered property (mal) because it is not acquired through permissible means and cannot be precisely measured or delivered in a sale contract.
The blank in the manuscript prevents full discussion, but the ruling remains definitive.
3
Acknowledge the textual dispute
The commentator mentions a contradictory transmission (عكس هذا الحكم) that might permit the sale, but he clarifies that the relied-upon version is the prohibition. The mufta bihi is the prohibition.
This dispute is about the authenticity of the transmission, not a difference in legal reasoning.

Selling an Absconding Slave: Automatic Rescission or Buyer’s Choice?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on automatic rescission of sale of absconding slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding automatic rescission of a sale of an absconding slave and state the preferred (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
The sale of an absconding slave is not automatically rescinded because the price substitutes for the lost item.

A buyer purchases an absconding slave on the condition that the slave is with the buyer. But the slave dies before delivery. Is the contract automatically void? Or does the buyer have a choice? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. This lesson examines the arguments of two positions and identifies the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The central question: if an absconding slave is sold and then perishes (or is lost) before the buyer takes possession, is the sale automatically rescinded, or does it remain valid until the buyer chooses rescission?
The dispute hinges on the interpretation of Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Understand the literal statement of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad states: 'If the seller does not have evidence and does not hand over the slave until it perishes, the sale is rescinded.' Some early Hanafi scholars took this literally to mean automatic rescission regardless of the buyer's will.
This view is recorded in al-Dhakhirah as one opinion.
3
Analyse the alternative interpretation
Later scholars (e.g., in al-Mi'raj and al-Dhakhirah's preferred view) argue that automatic rescission does not apply because the sale has a substitute (the price). The contract should not dissolve unless the buyer chooses to rescind. They reinterpret Muhammad's statement as meaning rescission upon the buyer's choice.
The key principle: 'if the sold item is lost but a substitute exists, the sale is not rescinded without choice.' This is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If the slave perishes and the buyer does not choose rescission, the buyer must pay the price and has no claim against the seller. If the sale were automatically rescinded, the buyer would not owe the price.
The dispute affects who bears the risk of loss before delivery.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that the sale is not automatically rescinded; the buyer must choose rescission. This is because the price serves as a substitute, and the condition of ability to deliver is met if the buyer claims the slave is with him.
This is the position adopted by later Hanafi authorities such as those cited in al-Dhakhirah and al-Mi'raj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن جحده وكان للمغصوب منه بينة عادلة فكذلك الجواب. وإن لم يكن له بينة ولم يسلمه انتقض البيع وبعض مشايخنا قالوا : قول محمد في الكتاب وإن لم يكن للمغصوب منه بينة ولم يسلمه حتى هلك انتقض البيع بظاهره غير صحيح، وينبغي أن لا ينتقض البيع لأن البيع وإن فات فقد أخلف بدلاً والمبيع إذا فات وأخلف بدلاً لا ينتقض البيع إلا أن يختار المشتري النقض فكان تأويل قول محمد انتقض البيع إذا اختار المشتري. وبعضهم قالوا: إنه بظاهره صحيح وينتقض البيع من غير اختيار المشتري إلى آخر ما في الذخيرة. وقيد ببيعه لأن هبته جائزة كما قدمناه على المعراج، وأما إعتاقه فجائز لكن إن أعتقه عن كفارة عليه فإنه لا يجوز حتى تعلم حياته كما في المعراج، ويصح جعله بدل خلع كما قدمناه في بابه عند قوله ولو اختلعت على عبد أبق لها على أنها بريئة من ضمانه لم تبرأ وأما جعله بدل صلح>> (۱) .
قوله : (إلا أن يبيعه ممن يزعم أنه عنده فيجوز البيع لأن المنهي عنه بيع آبق مطلق وهو أن يكون آبقاً في حقهما وهذا غير آبق في حق المشتري، ولأنه إذا كان عند المشتري انتفى العجز عن التسليم وهو المانع. ولم يذكر المصنف أنه يكتفي بقبضه عن قبض المبيع للتفصيل قالوا : إن كان أشهد وقت أخذه أنه أخذه ليرده على مالكه كان أمانه في يده فلا ينوب عن قبض البيع، فلو هلك قبل أن يصل إلى سيده لم يضمنه فينفسخ البيع ويرجع على سيده بالثمن، ولو كان لم يشهد صار قابضاً لأنه قبض غصب ؛ هكذا اقتصر الشارحون هنا. وذكر في الذخيرة : إذا اشترى ما أمانة هو في يده من وديعة أو عارية فإنه لا يكون قابضاً إلا إذا ذهب المودع أو المستعير إلى العين وانتهى إلى مكان يتمكن من قبضه الآن يصير المشتري قابضاً بالتخلية، فإذا هلك بعد ذلك يهلك من مال المشتري، فإن فعل المشتري في فصل الوديعة والعارية ما يكون قبضاً ثم أراد البائع أن يحبسها بالثمن لم يكن له ذلك لأنه لما باعه منه علمه أن المبيع في يد المشتري وهو يتمكن من القبض يصير راضياً بقبض المشتري دلالة اهـ. وقيد ببيعه ممن يزعم أنه عنده لأنه لو باعه من رجل يزعم أنه عند آخر فإنه لا يصح فاسد إذا قبضه المشتري ملكه بخلاف بيع الآبق فإنه باطل فلذا كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية أن بيع الآبق يكون باطلاً وفاسداً وصحيحاً
If he denies it and the victim of usurpation has just witnesses, the answer is likewise. And if he does not have evidence and does not hand it over, the sale is rescinded. Some of our teachers said: Muhammad's statement in the book 'And if the victim does not have evidence and does not hand it over until it perishes, the sale is rescinded' is not correct in its literal sense, and it should not be rescinded because the sale, even though it has been lost, has been replaced by a substitute. When the sold item is lost and a substitute is provided, the sale is not rescinded unless the buyer chooses rescission. Thus the interpretation of Muhammad's statement is that the sale is rescinded if the buyer chooses. And some said: it is correct in its literal sense and the sale is rescinded without the buyer's choice, as in al-Dhakhirah. He conditioned it on sale because gifting it is permissible as we previously mentioned on al-Mi'raj. As for manumitting it, it is permissible, but if he manumits it as expiation for a vow, it is not valid until his life is known as in al-Mi'raj. And it is valid to make it as a substitute for khul' as we mentioned in its chapter at his statement: 'If she made khul' for an absconding slave with the condition that she is free from his guarantee, she is not free.' And as for making it a substitute for sulh. (1) blank space. His statement: 'Except if he sells it to someone who claims that it is with him, then the sale is valid because the prohibition is selling an absconding slave absolutely, which is that it is absconding in the rights of both parties. And this is not absconding in the right of the buyer. And also because if it is with the buyer, the inability to deliver is removed, which is the impediment. The author did not mention that taking possession of it suffices for possession of the sold item. For detail, they said: If he had witnesses at the time of taking it that he took it to return it to its owner, it is a trust in his hand, so it does not substitute for possession of the sale. If it perishes before reaching its master, he is not liable, the sale is dissolved, and he returns to its master the price. But if he did not have witnesses, he becomes a possessor because it is a usurpation possession. The commentators limited it here. And in al-Dhakhirah: If he buys something that is already in his hand as a trust, like a deposit or a loan, he does not become a possessor unless the depositor or borrower goes to the item and reaches a place where he can now take possession, then the buyer becomes a possessor by vacating. If it perishes after that, it perishes from the buyer's wealth. If the buyer does in the chapter of deposit and loan what constitutes possession, then the seller wants to detain it for the price, he cannot, because when he sold it to him, he knew that the sold item is in the buyer's hand and he is able to take possession, so he is impliedly satisfied with the buyer's possession. End. And he conditioned it on selling to someone who claims it is with him because if he sells it to a man who claims it is with another, it is not valid as fasid. If the buyer takes possession, he owns it, unlike the sale of an absconding slave, which is batil. Hence we wrote in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah that the sale of an absconding slave can be batil, fasid, and sahih.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of selling an absconding slave (abaq). The core issue is whether the sale is automatically rescinded when the slave perishes without the buyer's knowledge or whether the buyer must choose rescission. The text presents two interpretations of Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir: one group says the sale is rescinded automatically, another says it is only rescinded if the buyer chooses. The preferred view is that rescission requires the buyer's choice because the sale has been replaced by a substitute (the price). The passage also discusses conditions for validity: if the buyer claims the slave is with him, the sale is valid because the prohibition applies only when the slave is absconding in the eyes of both parties. The commentary on the matn explains that the author's restriction 'except if he sells it to someone who claims it is with him' is key. Additionally, the text addresses issues of possession (qabd): if the buyer takes the slave with the intention to return it, it remains a trust; otherwise, it is a possession. The discussion includes references to al-Dhakhirah and other sources, clarifying that selling an absconding slave can be categorized as batil, fasid, or sahih depending on circumstances.

Key Terms
آبق (ābiq): An absconding slave who has run away from his master.
انتقض البيع (intaqaḍa al-bayʿ): The sale is rescinded or dissolved.
خلف بدلاً (akhlaṭ badalan): To provide a substitute (i.e., the price) in place of the lost subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is automatically rescinded regardless.
B) The buyer must choose to rescind the sale.
C) The seller must refund the price immediately.
D) The sale becomes fasid and is void.

Key Takeaway
The sale of an absconding slave is not automatically rescinded upon loss; the buyer has the option to rescind or keep the contract.

Selling a Woman's Milk: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling a woman's milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a woman's milk and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A woman's milk is part of an honored human; it cannot be sold, even if separated.

This lesson examines the prohibition of selling a woman's milk according to the Hanafi school. The source passage, from al-Bahr al-Raiq, discusses the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah and presents the dissenting view of Abu Yusuf regarding slave women. We analyze the proofs, the response, and the application to medical treatment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The text states the sale is not permissible because the human is honored. The basis is the principle that a human and all its parts are inviolable and not property.
This ruling applies to both free and slave women in the apparent narration.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues by analogy: if selling a slave woman herself is permissible, then selling her part (milk) should also be permissible.
His qiyas relies on the idea that the milk is a part of something that can be sold.
3
Trace the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes: slavery affects the person herself, but milk has no life and cannot be a locus of ownership. Thus the analogy fails.
The lack of life in milk is key – it cannot be manumitted or owned.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The majority holds that the sale contract is fasid (voidable). Abu Yusuf would consider it valid for a slave woman. The relied-upon position is prohibition.
This affects actual transactions and liability for destroying the milk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولبن) (امرأة بالجر أي لم يجز بيع لبن المرأة لأنه جزء الآدمي وهو بجميع أجزائه مكرم مصون عن الابتذال بالبيع، أطلقه فشمل لبن الحرة والأمة وهو ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف يجوز بيع لبن الأمة لجواز إيراد البيع على نفسها فكذا على جزئها . قلنا : الرق حل نفسها فأما اللبن فلا رق فيه لأنه يختص بمحل يتحقق فيه القوة التي ضده وهي الحي ولا حياة في اللبن فلا يكون محلاً للعتق ولا للرق فكذا البيع، فشمل ما إذا كان في إناء أو لا، والأولى أن يقيد مراده بما إذا كان في وعاء كما قيده في الهداية لأن حكم اللبن في الضرع قد تقدم، وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا يضمن متلفه لكونه ليس بمال وإلى أنه لا يحل به التداوي في العين الرمداء وفيه قولان: فقيل بالمنع، وقيل بالجواز إذا علم فيه الشفاء. هكذا في فتح القدير هنا. وقال في موضع آخر : وأهل الطب يثبتون نفعاً للبن البنت للعين وهذه من أفراد مسألة الانتفاع بالمحرم للتداوي كالخمر. واختار في الخانية والنهاية الجواز إذا علم أن فيه الشفاء ولم يجد دواء غيره وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى تمامه في الحظر والإباحة وقيد بلبن المرأة لأنه يجوز بيع لبن الأنعام . قال الإمام الرباني محمد بن الحسن الشيباني : جواز إجارة الظئر دليل على فساد بيع لبنها وجواز بيع لبن الأنعام دليل على فساد إجارتها.
قوله : (كما قيده في الهداية أي حيث قال في قدح قال في النهر : وهذا القيد لبيان منع بيعه بعد انفصاله عن محله كيلا يظن أن امتناع بيعه ما دام في الضرع كغيره ؛ كذا في الفتح. وقال في الحواشي السعدية وهذا بعيد جداً بعدما تقدم أن بيع اللبن في الضرع لا يجوز اهـ. وبيانه أن امتناع بيعه في الضرع قد علم ما مر فذكر منع بيع لبن المرأة بعده نص في المنع بعد الانفصال فلا حاجة إلى التقييد به، وبه اندفع ما في البحر من أن ذكره أولى لأن حكم اللبن في الضرع قد تقدم على أنا لا نسلم أنه مستفاد مما تقدم بما قدمناه من أن الضرع خاص بذوات الأربع كالثدي للمرأة، وحينئذ فإنما أطلقه المصنف ليعم ما قبل الانفصال وما بعده.
His statement: 'And milk of a woman' (with genitive case) meaning the sale of a woman's milk is not permissible because it is a part of a human, and a human with all his parts is honored, protected from being demeaned by sale. He (the author) made it absolute, so it includes the milk of a free woman and a slave woman, and this is the apparent narration. From Abu Yusuf: the sale of a slave woman's milk is permissible because it is permissible to contract a sale on herself, so likewise on her part. We say: slavery encompasses herself, but as for milk, there is no slavery in it because it is specific to a place where there is a force opposite to it, which is life, and there is no life in milk, so it is not a locus for manumission or slavery, so likewise for sale. So it includes when it is in a container or not. It is better to restrict his intention to when it is in a vessel, as he restricted it in al-Hidayah, because the ruling of milk in the udder has preceded. The author indicated that its destroyer is not liable because it is not property, and that it is not permissible to treat with it for ophthalmia, but there are two opinions: some say prohibition, some say permissibility if healing is known. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And he said elsewhere: Medical doctors affirm a benefit of a daughter's milk for the eye, and this is one of the issues of benefiting from prohibited things for treatment like wine. In al-Khaniyyah and al-Nihayah, they chose permissibility if it is known that there is healing and no other medicine is found. This will come later in al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah. And he restricted it to a woman's milk because the sale of animal milk is permissible. Imam al-Rabbani Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani said: The permissibility of hiring a wet nurse is evidence of the invalidity of selling her milk, and the permissibility of selling animal milk is evidence of the invalidity of hiring them.
His statement: 'As he restricted it in al-Hidayah' i.e., where he said in Qadih: In al-Nahr: This restriction is to explain the prohibition of its sale after it separates from its place, lest one think that its prohibition is only while in the udder like others. Thus in al-Fath. And in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah, this is very far-fetched after what was mentioned that the sale of milk in the udder is not permissible. Its explanation: The prohibition of its sale in the udder is known from what has passed, so mentioning the prohibition of selling a woman's milk afterwards is a text for prohibition after separation, so there is no need for the restriction. By this, what is in al-Bahr that its mention is better is refuted because the ruling of milk in the udder had preceded, but we do not concede that it is derived from what preceded by what we have presented that the udder is specific to quadrupeds like the breast for women. Then the author made it absolute to include both before and after separation.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the sale of a woman's milk. The general ruling (from Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is not permissible because it is part of a human being, which is inviolable and not to be bought and sold. Abu Yusuf, however, allows the sale of a slave woman's milk by analogy to selling her herself. The response is that slavery applies to the person, not the milk, as milk has no life and thus cannot be owned or manumitted. The text also discusses the issue of using milk for medicinal purposes: there are two opinions, with the chosen view being that it is permissible if healing is known and no alternative exists. The commentary on the matn from al-Hidayah clarifies that the prohibition applies whether the milk is in the container or still in the breast, rejecting the need to restrict the ruling to after separation. The passage concludes with Imam Muhammad's insight: the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse actually proves the prohibition of selling her milk, while the permissibility of selling animal milk proves the prohibition of hiring them.

Key Terms
الآدمي مكرم (al-ādamī mukarram): The human being is honored and inviolable; therefore, selling parts of a human is not allowed.
ظئر (ẓī'r): A wet nurse (woman who breastfeeds another's child).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for the Hanafi prohibition of selling a woman's milk?
A) The milk is impure.
B) The milk is part of an honored human being and not property.
C) The milk causes harm to the baby.
D) There is no demand for it.

Key Takeaway
The sale of a woman's milk is prohibited in the Hanafi school because it is part of an honored human being; the dissenting view of Abu Yusuf is not relied upon.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling Pig Hair: Prohibition and Permissibility of Use
Explaining prohibition of sale and permitting use under necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why selling pig hair is haram in the Hanafi school and distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding its use.

Core Idea
Selling pig hair is haram to humiliate it; using it is only restricted if it remains impure.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on pig hair. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses why selling pig hair is prohibited—not because it lacks value, but because selling it would honor something we are commanded to dishonor. At the same time, the passage addresses the permissibility of using pig hair for stitching leather, and introduces a key disagreement within the Hanafi school between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani over whether pig hair is inherently impure. This dispute has practical consequences for when its use is restricted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Determine what the passage says about selling pig hair and the reasoning provided.
The ruling is prohibition (haram) based on the principle of humiliation (ihānah).
2
Understand the ʿilla (legal cause)
Analyze the analogy with wine, pig, and a woman's milk to see how the same act (sale) can be honor or humiliation depending on the object.
The ʿilla is the command to humiliate the pig and its parts; sale would contradict that.
3
Examine the permissibility of use
Note that the passage permits using pig hair for stitching (khurz) under necessity, refuting the idea that prohibition of sale implies prohibition of use.
Use is permissible even if the substance is impure, as long as there is necessity.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement between Abu Yusuf (najis) and Muhammad (tahir) on the impurity of pig hair, and how it affects the conditions of use.
The restriction to necessity hinges on Abu Yusuf's view; Muhammad's view removes the restriction.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: if pig hair is pure (Muhammad), it can be used freely; if impure (Abu Yusuf), only for necessity.
Later Hanafi works tend to favor Muhammad's view, but both are transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وشعر الخنزير أي لم يجز بيعه إهانة له لكونه نجس العين كأصله فالبيع هنا لو جاز لكان إكراماً وفي الخمر والخنزير كذلك لو جاز لكان إعزازاً وقد أمرنا بالإهانة، وفي لبن المرأة لو جاز لكان إهانة لها وقد أمرنا بإعزاز الآدمي فالفعل الواحد وهو البيع هنا يجوز أن يكون إعزازاً بالنسبة إلى محل وإهانة بالنسبة إلى آخر مثلاً إذا أمر السلطان بعض الغلمان بالوقوف عند الفرس بحضرته كان إعزازاً له، ولو أمر القاضي بذلك لكان إهانة له. وحاصله أن جواز بيع المهان إعزاز له وجواز بيع المكرم إهانة له قوله : (وينتفع به) أي يجوز الانتفاع بشعر الخنزير دفعاً لما يتوهم من منع بيعه ولكنه مقيد بالخرز للضرورة فإن ذلك العمل لا يتأتي بدونه ويوجد مباحاً فلا حاجة إلى القول يجواز بيعه وشرائه حتى لو لم يوجد لم يكره القاضي قوله : (كما قيده في الهداية أي حيث قال في قدح قال في النهر : وهذا القيد لبيان منع بيعه بعد انفصاله عن محله كيلا يظن أن امتناع بيعه ما دام في الضرع كغيره ؛ كذا في الفتح. وقال في الحواشي السعدية وهذا بعيد جداً بعدما تقدم أن بيع اللبن في الضرع لا يجوز اهـ. وبيانه أن امتناع بيعه في الضرع قد علم ما مر فذكر منع بيع لبن المرأة بعده نص في المنع بعد الانفصال فلا حاجة إلى التقييد به، وبه اندفع ما في البحر من أن ذكره أولى لأن حكم اللبن في الضرع قد تقدم على أنا لا نسلم أنه مستفاد مما تقدم بما قدمناه من أن الضرع خاص بذوات الأربع كالثدي للمرأة، وحينئذ فإنما أطلقه المصنف ليعم ما قبل الانفصال وما بعده. قوله : (ولكنه مقيد بالخرز للضرورة) هذا بناء على قول أبي يوسف بنجاسته؛ أما على قول محمد الآتي من أنه طاهر فلا يتقيد الانتفاع به بالخرز ولا
His statement: 'And pig hair' meaning its sale is not permissible, as a humiliation for it because it is inherently impure like its origin. If its sale were permissible, it would be an honor. Similarly for wine and pig, if sale were permissible, it would be a glorification, and we are commanded to humiliate them. As for a woman's milk, if sale were permissible, it would be a humiliation for her, and we are commanded to honor the human. Thus a single act, namely sale, can be an honor in one context and a humiliation in another. For example, if the sultan orders some pages to stand by the horse in his presence, that is an honor for them; if the judge orders that, it is a humiliation. The summary is that permitting the sale of something contemptible is an honor for it, and permitting the sale of something honored is a humiliation for it. His statement: 'And benefit from it' meaning it is permissible to benefit from pig hair, refuting the misapprehension that its sale is prohibited. But it is restricted to [use for] stitching due to necessity, because that work cannot be done without it and it is found permissible. So there is no need to say its sale and purchase are permissible. Even if it is not found, it is not disliked. The judge said: His statement: 'As he restricted it in al-Hidayah' i.e., where he said in Qadih: In al-Nahr: This restriction is to explain the prohibition of its sale after it separates from its place, lest one think that its prohibition is only while in the udder like others. Thus in al-Fath. And in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah, this is very far-fetched after what was mentioned that the sale of milk in the udder is not permissible. Its explanation: The prohibition of its sale in the udder is known from what has passed, so mentioning the prohibition of selling a woman's milk afterwards is a text for prohibition after separation, so there is no need for the restriction. By this, what is in al-Bahr that its mention is better is refuted because the ruling of milk in the udder had preceded, but we do not concede that it is derived from what preceded by what we have presented that the udder is specific to quadrupeds like the breast for women. Then the author made it absolute to include both before and after separation. His statement: 'But it is restricted to stitching due to necessity.' This is based on Abu Yusuf's view that it is impure. But according to Muhammad's upcoming view that it is pure, then benefiting from it is not restricted to stitching, nor...
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of pig hair. The ruling is that selling pig hair is not permissible because it is inherently impure (najis al-'ayn), and selling it would imply honor, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the pig. The text draws an interesting analogy: the same act of sale can be a form of honor or humiliation depending on the object. For pig and wine, sale would honor them; for a woman's milk, sale would dishonor her. Hence the prohibition differs. However, using pig hair is permissible for necessity, specifically for stitching (khurz) leather, because that work often requires pig hair and no alternative exists. This use is permitted only if pig hair is considered impure (Abu Yusuf's view). If it is considered pure (Muhammad's view), then the restriction to necessity does not apply, and it can be used freely. The passage also includes a comment on al-Hidayah's restriction, which is actually about milk but seems to be brought here for comparison. The overall point is that the sale of pig hair is haram, but its use is permitted under necessity.

Key Terms
نجس العين (najis al-ʿayn): Inherently impure substance, whose sale is prohibited because it would imply honor.
الخرز (al-kharz): Stitching or sewing, especially of leather, often done with pig hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is selling pig hair prohibited?
A) Because it is harmful to health.
B) Because it is inherently impure and selling it would honor it, whereas we are commanded to humiliate it.
C) Because it is not considered wealth.
D) Because it is difficult to deliver.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of selling pig hair is based on the principle of humiliation, not impurity; its use is subject to the internal Hanafi dispute over its purity.
